# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed findings covering:

### **Kubernetes/Kubernetes**
- Uses a custom **KubeRegistry** wrapper with a sophisticated stability framework
- Key files: `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/registry.go` (main registry) and `legacyregistry/registry.go` (global registry)
- Features: Version-aware registration, deprecation lifecycle management, STABLE/BETA/ALPHA stability levels
- Metrics: `NewCounterVec()`, `NewHistogramVec()`, `NewGaugeVec()` with stability options

### **Grafana/Grafana**
- Uses **promauto** (prometheus auto-registration) pattern
- Key files: `pkg/services/ngalert/metrics/scheduler.go`, `pkg/infra/metrics/frontendmetrics.go`, metrics middleware
- Pattern: `promauto.With(registerer).New<MetricType>()` for automatic registration
- Flexible: Per-component registerers, chainable registration methods

### **Prometheus/Prometheus**
- Direct **prometheus.Registerer** interface usage
- Key files: `notifier/metric.go`, `tsdb/db.go`, `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, `cmd/prometheus/main.go`
- Pattern: Metric structs created in constructors, explicit `registerer.MustRegister()` calls
- Advanced: Supports `NewGaugeFunc()` for computed metrics, native histogram support

The answer includes **27 specific files**, **30 key symbols**, **call chains**, and a detailed narrative explaining each project's approach to metric registration.

Prometheus metrics are created, registered, and exposed in three major Go projects: Kubernetes, Grafana, and Prometheus itself. Each project uses different architectural approaches while leveraging the prometheus/client_golang library.\\n\\n### Kubernetes/Kubernetes: Custom Registry with Stability Framework\\n\\nKubernetes implements a sophisticated metric registration system through a custom `KubeRegistry` wrapper (kubernetes/kubernetes:staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/registry.go:KubeRegistry). This interface extends prometheus.Registry/prometheus.Registerer with additional capabilities for metric stability management and deprecation tracking.\\n\\n**Key Components:**\\n- **Registry Interface**: `KubeRegistry` defines MustRegister(), Register(), CustomMustRegister(), and CustomRegister() methods\\n- **Implementation**: `kubeRegistry` struct wraps prometheus.Registry with version tracking, hidden collectors, stable collectors, and resettable interfaces\\n- **Creation**: `NewKubeRegistry()` function creates instances with version information from the Kubernetes build\\n- **Global Registry**: `legacyregistry/registry.go:defaultRegistry` provides a singleton global registry\\n- **Metric Creators**: Uses `metrics.NewCounterVec()`, `metrics.NewHistogramVec()`, `metrics.NewGaugeVec()` with `CounterOpts`, `HistogramOpts`, `GaugeOpts` including `StabilityLevel` fields\\n\\n**Metric Registration Pattern**:\\n1. Metrics defined as package-level variables in `staging/src/k8s.io/endpointslice/metrics/metrics.go` and similar files\\n2. Metrics include stability levels (STABLE, BETA, ALPHA) for deprecation lifecycle management\\n3. Registration via `MustRegister()` which handles visibility based on version and stability\\n4. Handler exposed through `legacyregistry.Handler()` for HTTP endpoints\\n\\n**Example Files**:\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/endpointslice/metrics/metrics.go`: EndpointsDesired (GaugeVec), EndpointSliceSyncs (CounterVec)\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/metrics/metrics.go`: requestCounter (CounterVec), responseSizes (HistogramVec)\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/prometheus/workqueue/metrics.go`: depth, adds, unfinished metrics\\n\\n### Grafana/Grafana: Promauto Automatic Registration\\n\\nGrafana uses the `github.com/prometheus/client_golang/prometheus/promauto` package for automatic metric registration, combined with per-component metrics constructors that accept a `prometheus.Registerer`.\\n\\n**Key Components:**\\n- **Promauto Pattern**: `promauto.With(registerer).New<MetricType>()` for automatic registration with a specific registerer\\n- **Alternative Global Pattern**: `promauto.New<MetricType>()` for metrics registered to the default registerer\\n- **Metrics Structs**: Components define metrics in struct fields, initialized in constructor functions\\n- **Metrics Constructor**: Functions like `NewSchedulerMetrics(r prometheus.Registerer)` return metrics structs\\n- **Namespace/Subsystem**: Uses prometheus.CounterOpts, prometheus.HistogramOpts, prometheus.GaugeOpts with Name, Help, Namespace, Subsystem\\n\\n**Metric Registration Pattern**:\\n1. Components define a metrics struct containing counter, gauge, histogram, and histogram fields\\n2. Constructor function uses `promauto.With()` to wrap the registerer\\n3. Metrics are created inline in the constructor using `promauto.With(r).NewCounterVec()` etc.\\n4. Labels and options specified in prometheus.CounterOpts/HistogramOpts/GaugeOpts\\n5. Automatic registration happens on creation (promauto behavior)\\n\\n**Example Files**:\\n- `pkg/services/ngalert/metrics/scheduler.go`: NewSchedulerMetrics() with promauto.With(r).NewGauge(), NewCounterVec(), NewHistogramVec()\\n- `pkg/infra/metrics/frontendmetrics.go`: registerFrontendHistogram() with manual registration via reg.MustRegister()\\n- `pkg/infra/httpclient/httpclientprovider/prometheus_metrics_middleware.go`: NewPrometheusMetricsMiddleware() with manual register/MustRegister methods\\n- `pkg/services/ngalert/metrics/api.go`: NewAPI() with promauto pattern for request duration histograms\\n\\n### Prometheus/Prometheus: Direct Registration with Registerer Interface\\n\\nPrometheus itself uses direct instantiation of metric collectors with explicit registration via the prometheus.Registerer interface. Metrics are organized into struct-based collectors that are instantiated with constructor functions.\\n\\n**Key Components:**\\n- **Metric Structs**: Each component (notifier, tsdb, scrape, etc.) defines a struct holding its metrics\\n- **Constructor Functions**: Functions like `newAlertMetrics()`, `newDBMetrics()` create and optionally register metrics\\n- **Metric Creation**: Direct calls to `prometheus.NewCounter()`, `prometheus.NewHistogram()`, `prometheus.NewGaugeFunc()` etc.\\n- **Registration Methods**: `registerer.MustRegister()` for component registrars, `prometheus.MustRegister()` for global registrations\\n- **Gauge Functions**: Supports `prometheus.NewGaugeFunc()` for computed metrics that call a function on each scrape\\n\\n**Metric Registration Pattern**:\\n1. Metrics structs defined in package (e.g., `alertMetrics`, `dbMetrics`, `queueManagerMetrics`)\\n2. Constructor function creates all metric instances using `prometheus.New<Type>(prometheus.<Type>Opts{})`\\n3. If registerer provided, metrics registered with `r.MustRegister(metric1, metric2, ...)`\\n4. Metrics include namespace, subsystem, name, help, and sometimes custom labels or buckets\\n5. GaugeFunc allows dynamic values computed at scrape time\\n\\n**Example Files**:\\n- `notifier/metric.go`: newAlertMetrics() creates alertMetrics struct with SummaryVec, HistogramVec, CounterVec, GaugeVec, GaugeFunc\\n- `tsdb/db.go`: newDBMetrics() creates dbMetrics with NewCounter(), NewGauge(), NewHistogram(), NewGaugeFunc()\\n- `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`: queueManagerMetrics constructor with extensive gauges and counters\\n- `cmd/prometheus/main.go`: Global MustRegister() calls for configSuccess and configSuccessTime metrics\\n- `web/web.go`: newMetrics() with requestCounter, requestDuration, responseSize, readyStatus\\n- `rules/group.go`: GroupMetrics struct with counters, gauges, histograms for rule evaluation\\n\\n### Key Differences Summary\\n\\n**Registration Approach**:\\n- Kubernetes: Custom KubeRegistry wrapper with version-aware registration\\n- Grafana: Promauto automatic registration with per-component registerers\\n- Prometheus: Explicit registration via prometheus.Registerer interface\\n\\n**Metric Organization**:\\n- Kubernetes: Package-level variables, global legacy registry, stability levels\\n- Grafana: Component metrics structs, promauto in constructors\\n- Prometheus: Component metrics structs, manual registration in constructors\\n\\n**Registration Triggers**:\\n- Kubernetes: Explicit MustRegister() calls during initialization\\n- Grafana: Automatic via promauto during metric creation\\n- Prometheus: Explicit MustRegister() during component construction or main()\\n\\n**Extensibility**:\\n- Kubernetes: Stability framework, deprecation management, version-based visibility\\n- Grafana: Flexible namespace/subsystem configuration, chainable registration\\n- Prometheus: Direct control, GaugeFunc for computed metrics, native histogram support\"\n}\n",

Prometheus metrics are created, registered, and exposed in three major Go projects: Kubernetes, Grafana, and Prometheus itself. Each project uses different architectural approaches while leveraging the prometheus/client_golang library.\\n\\n### Kubernetes/Kubernetes: Custom Registry with Stability Framework\\n\\nKubernetes implements a sophisticated metric registration system through a custom `KubeRegistry` wrapper (kubernetes/kubernetes:staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/registry.go:KubeRegistry). This interface extends prometheus.Registry/prometheus.Registerer with additional capabilities for metric stability management and deprecation tracking.\\n\\n**Key Components:**\\n- **Registry Interface**: `KubeRegistry` defines MustRegister(), Register(), CustomMustRegister(), and CustomRegister() methods\\n- **Implementation**: `kubeRegistry` struct wraps prometheus.Registry with version tracking, hidden collectors, stable collectors, and resettable interfaces\\n- **Creation**: `NewKubeRegistry()` function creates instances with version information from the Kubernetes build\\n- **Global Registry**: `legacyregistry/registry.go:defaultRegistry` provides a singleton global registry\\n- **Metric Creators**: Uses `metrics.NewCounterVec()`, `metrics.NewHistogramVec()`, `metrics.NewGaugeVec()` with `CounterOpts`, `HistogramOpts`, `GaugeOpts` including `StabilityLevel` fields\\n\\n**Metric Registration Pattern**:\\n1. Metrics defined as package-level variables in `staging/src/k8s.io/endpointslice/metrics/metrics.go` and similar files\\n2. Metrics include stability levels (STABLE, BETA, ALPHA) for deprecation lifecycle management\\n3. Registration via `MustRegister()` which handles visibility based on version and stability\\n4. Handler exposed through `legacyregistry.Handler()` for HTTP endpoints\\n\\n**Example Files**:\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/endpointslice/metrics/metrics.go`: EndpointsDesired (GaugeVec), EndpointSliceSyncs (CounterVec)\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/metrics/metrics.go`: requestCounter (CounterVec), responseSizes (HistogramVec)\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/prometheus/workqueue/metrics.go`: depth, adds, unfinished metrics\\n\\n### Grafana/Grafana: Promauto Automatic Registration\\n\\nGrafana uses the `github.com/prometheus/client_golang/prometheus/promauto` package for automatic metric registration, combined with per-component metrics constructors that accept a `prometheus.Registerer`.\\n\\n**Key Components:**\\n- **Promauto Pattern**: `promauto.With(registerer).New<MetricType>()` for automatic registration with a specific registerer\\n- **Alternative Global Pattern**: `promauto.New<MetricType>()` for metrics registered to the default registerer\\n- **Metrics Structs**: Components define metrics in struct fields, initialized in constructor functions\\n- **Metrics Constructor**: Functions like `NewSchedulerMetrics(r prometheus.Registerer)` return metrics structs\\n- **Namespace/Subsystem**: Uses prometheus.CounterOpts, prometheus.HistogramOpts, prometheus.GaugeOpts with Name, Help, Namespace, Subsystem\\n\\n**Metric Registration Pattern**:\\n1. Components define a metrics struct containing counter, gauge, histogram, and histogram fields\\n2. Constructor function uses `promauto.With()` to wrap the registerer\\n3. Metrics are created inline in the constructor using `promauto.With(r).NewCounterVec()` etc.\\n4. Labels and options specified in prometheus.CounterOpts/HistogramOpts/GaugeOpts\\n5. Automatic registration happens on creation (promauto behavior)\\n\\n**Example Files**:\\n- `pkg/services/ngalert/metrics/scheduler.go`: NewSchedulerMetrics() with promauto.With(r).NewGauge(), NewCounterVec(), NewHistogramVec()\\n- `pkg/infra/metrics/frontendmetrics.go`: registerFrontendHistogram() with manual registration via reg.MustRegister()\\n- `pkg/infra/httpclient/httpclientprovider/prometheus_metrics_middleware.go`: NewPrometheusMetricsMiddleware() with manual register/MustRegister methods\\n- `pkg/services/ngalert/metrics/api.go`: NewAPI() with promauto pattern for request duration histograms\\n\\n### Prometheus/Prometheus: Direct Registration with Registerer Interface\\n\\nPrometheus itself uses direct instantiation of metric collectors with explicit registration via the prometheus.Registerer interface. Metrics are organized into struct-based collectors that are instantiated with constructor functions.\\n\\n**Key Components:**\\n- **Metric Structs**: Each component (notifier, tsdb, scrape, etc.) defines a struct holding its metrics\\n- **Constructor Functions**: Functions like `newAlertMetrics()`, `newDBMetrics()` create and optionally register metrics\\n- **Metric Creation**: Direct calls to `prometheus.NewCounter()`, `prometheus.NewHistogram()`, `prometheus.NewGaugeFunc()` etc.\\n- **Registration Methods**: `registerer.MustRegister()` for component registrars, `prometheus.MustRegister()` for global registrations\\n- **Gauge Functions**: Supports `prometheus.NewGaugeFunc()` for computed metrics that call a function on each scrape\\n\\n**Metric Registration Pattern**:\\n1. Metrics structs defined in package (e.g., `alertMetrics`, `dbMetrics`, `queueManagerMetrics`)\\n2. Constructor function creates all metric instances using `prometheus.New<Type>(prometheus.<Type>Opts{})`\\n3. If registerer provided, metrics registered with `r.MustRegister(metric1, metric2, ...)`\\n4. Metrics include namespace, subsystem, name, help, and sometimes custom labels or buckets\\n5. GaugeFunc allows dynamic values computed at scrape time\\n\\n**Example Files**:\\n- `notifier/metric.go`: newAlertMetrics() creates alertMetrics struct with SummaryVec, HistogramVec, CounterVec, GaugeVec, GaugeFunc\\n- `tsdb/db.go`: newDBMetrics() creates dbMetrics with NewCounter(), NewGauge(), NewHistogram(), NewGaugeFunc()\\n- `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`: queueManagerMetrics constructor with extensive gauges and counters\\n- `cmd/prometheus/main.go`: Global MustRegister() calls for configSuccess and configSuccessTime metrics\\n- `web/web.go`: newMetrics() with requestCounter, requestDuration, responseSize, readyStatus\\n- `rules/group.go`: GroupMetrics struct with counters, gauges, histograms for rule evaluation\\n\\n### Key Differences Summary\\n\\n**Registration Approach**:\\n- Kubernetes: Custom KubeRegistry wrapper with version-aware registration\\n- Grafana: Promauto automatic registration with per-component registerers\\n- Prometheus: Explicit registration via prometheus.Registerer interface\\n\\n**Metric Organization**:\\n- Kubernetes: Package-level variables, global legacy registry, stability levels\\n- Grafana: Component metrics structs, promauto in constructors\\n- Prometheus: Component metrics structs, manual registration in constructors\\n\\n**Registration Triggers**:\\n- Kubernetes: Explicit MustRegister() calls during initialization\\n- Grafana: Automatic via promauto during metric creation\\n- Prometheus: Explicit MustRegister() during component construction or main()\\n\\n**Extensibility**:\\n- Kubernetes: Stability framework, deprecation management, version-based visibility\\n- Grafana: Flexible namespace/subsystem configuration, chainable registration\\n- Prometheus: Direct control, GaugeFunc for computed metrics, native histogram support\"\n}\n",
